top-level domain">Internet TLD</a></th><td>\n<a href="/wiki/.ie" title=".ie">.ie</a><sup class="reference" id="ref_tld"><a href="#endnote_tld">[b]</a></sup></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="text-align:left;margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;"><ol style="list-style-type: lower-alpha; margin-left: 1em; font-size:90%;">\n<li value="1"><span that the name of the state is <i>Ireland</i>; <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.irishstatutebook.ie/1948/en/act/pub/0022/sec0002.html#zza22y1948s2">Section 2</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland_Act_1948" title="Republic of Ireland Act 1948">Republic of Ireland Act 1948</a> declares that <i>Republic of Ireland</i> is "the description of the State".<sup id="cite_ref-Coakley2009_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Coakley2009-8">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup></li><li value="2"><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_tld"><b><a href="#ref_tld">^</a></b></span>  The <a href="/wiki/.eu" title=".eu">.eu</a> domain is also used, as it is shared with other European Union member states.</li>\n</ol></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Ireland</b> (<a href="/wiki/Irish_language" title="Irish language">Irish</a>: <i lang="ga">\xc3\x89ire</i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Irish" title="Help:IPA/Irish">[\xcb\x88e\xcb\x90\xc9\xbe\xca\xb2\xc9\x99]</a></span><small class="nowrap">&#160;(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Eire_pronunciation.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a>&#160;</span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e0/Eire_pronunciation.ogg" class="internal" title="Eire pronunciation.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small>), also known as the <b>Republic of Ireland</b> (<i><i lang="ga" title="Irish language text">Poblacht na h\xc3\x89ireann</i></i>), is a country in north-western <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> occupying 26 of 32 counties of the <a href="/wiki/Island_of_Ireland" class="mw-redirect" title="Island of Ireland">island of Ireland</a>. The capital and largest city is <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin</a>, which is located on the eastern part of the island, and whose metropolitan area is home to around a third of the country\'s 4.8 million inhabitants. The <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign state</a> shares its only land border with <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Countries_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Countries of the United Kingdom">part</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>. It is otherwise surrounded by the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a>, with the <a href="/wiki/Celtic_Sea" title="Celtic Sea">Celtic Sea</a> to the south, <a href="/wiki/Saint_George%27s_Channel" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint George&#39;s Channel">Saint George\'s Channel</a> to the south-east, and the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Sea" title="Irish Sea">Irish Sea</a> to the east. It is a <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">unitary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_republic" title="Parliamentary republic">parliamentary republic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> The legislature, the <i><i lang="ga" title="Irish language text"><a href="/wiki/Oireachtas" title="Oireachtas">Oireachtas</a></i></i>, consists of a <a href="/wiki/Lower_house" title="Lower house">lower house</a>, <i><i lang="ga" title="Irish language text"><a href="/wiki/D%C3%A1il_%C3%89ireann" title="D\xc3\xa1il \xc3\x89ireann">D\xc3\xa1il \xc3\x89ireann</a></i></i>, an <a href="/wiki/Upper_house" title="Upper house">upper house</a>, <i><i lang="ga" title="Irish language text"><a href="/wiki/Seanad_%C3%89ireann" title="Seanad \xc3\x89ireann">Seanad \xc3\x89ireann</a></i></i>, and an elected <a href="/wiki/President_of_Ireland" title="President of Ireland">President</a> (<i><i lang="ga" title="Irish language text">Uachtar\xc3\xa1n</i></i>) who serves as the largely ceremonial <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a>, but with some important powers and duties. The <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a> is the <i><i lang="ga" title="Irish language text"><a href="/wiki/Taoiseach" title="Taoiseach">Taoiseach</a></i></i> (Prime Minister, literally \'Chief\', a title not used in English), who is elected by the D\xc3\xa1il and appointed by the President; the Taoiseach in turn appoints other government ministers.\n</p><p>The state was created as the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Free_State" title="Irish Free State">Irish Free State</a> in 1922 as a result of the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Irish_Treaty" title="Anglo-Irish Treaty">Anglo-Irish Treaty</a>. It had the status of <a href="/wiki/Dominion" title="Dominion">Dominion</a> until 1937 when a <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Ireland" title="Constitution of Ireland">new constitution</a> was adopted, in which the state was named "Ireland" and effectively became a republic, with an elected non-executive president as head of state. It was officially declared a republic in 1949, following the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland_Act_1948" title="Republic of Ireland Act 1948">Republic of Ireland Act 1948</a>. Ireland became a member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> in December 1955. It joined the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Community" title="European Economic Community">European Economic Community</a> (EEC), the predecessor of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, in 1973. The state had no formal relations with Northern Ireland for most of the twentieth century, but during the 1980s and 1990s the British and Irish governments worked with the Northern Ireland parties towards a resolution to "<a href="/wiki/The_Troubles" title="The Troubles">the Troubles</a>". Since the signing of the <a href="/wiki/Good_Friday_Agreement" title="Good Friday Agreement">Good Friday Agreement</a> in 1998, the <a href="/wiki/Irish_government" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish government">Irish government</a> and <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_Executive" title="Northern Ireland Executive">Northern Ireland Executive</a> have co-operated on a number of policy areas under the <a href="/wiki/North-South_Ministerial_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="North-South Ministerial Council">North-South Ministerial Council</a> created by the Agreement.\n</p><p>Ireland ranks among the top twenty-five wealthiest countries in the world in terms of GDP per capita,<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> and as the tenth most prosperous country in the world according to The Legatum Prosperity Index 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-Legatum_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Legatum-11">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> After joining the EEC, Ireland enacted a series of <a href="/wiki/Economic_liberalism" title="Economic liberalism">liberal economic policies</a> that resulted in rapid economic growth. The country achieved considerable prosperity between the years of 1995 and 2007, which became known as the <a href="/wiki/Celtic_Tiger" title="Celtic Tiger">Celtic Tiger</a> period. This was halted by an unprecedented <a href="/wiki/Post-2008_Irish_economic_downturn" title="Post-2008 Irish economic downturn">financial crisis</a> that began in 2008, in conjunction with the concurrent <a href="/wiki/Financial_crisis_of_2007%E2%80%9308" class="mw-redirect" title="Financial crisis of 2007\xe2\x80\x9308">global economic crash</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-workforall_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-workforall-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> However, as the Irish economy was the fastest growing in the EU in 2015,<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Ireland is again quickly ascending league tables comparing wealth and prosperity internationally. For example, in 2015, Ireland was ranked as the joint sixth (with <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>) most developed country in the world by the United Nations <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> It also performs well in several national performance metrics, including <a href="/wiki/Press_Freedom_Index" title="Press Freedom Index">freedom of the press</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_economic_freedom" title="List of countries by economic freedom">economic freedom</a> and <a href="/wiki/Freedom_in_the_World" title="Freedom in the World">civil liberties</a>. Ireland is a member of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> and is a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">Council of Europe</a> and the <a href="/wiki/OECD" title="OECD">OECD</a>. The Irish government has followed a policy of military <a href="/wiki/Neutrality_(international_relations)" class="mw-redirect" title="Neutrality (international relations)">neutrality</a> through non-alignment since immediately prior to <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> and the country is consequently not a member of <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> although it is a member of <a href="/wiki/Partnership_for_Peace" title="Partnership for Peace">Partnership for Peace</a>.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" class="toctext">Climate</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-10"><a href="#Politics"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Politics</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-11"><a href="#Local_government"><span class="tocnumber">4.1</span> <span class="toctext">Local government</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-12"><a href="#Law"><span class="tocnumber">4.2</span> <span class="toctext">Law</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-13"><a href="#Foreign_relations"><span class="tocnumber">4.3</span> <span class="toctext">Foreign relations</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-14"><a href="#Military"><span class="tocnumber">4.4</span> <span class="toctext">Military</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-15"><a href="#Economy"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Economy</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-16"><a href="#Taxation_policy"><span class="tocnumber">5.1</span> <span class="toctext">Taxation policy</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-17"><a href="#Trade"><span class="tocnumber">5.2</span> <span class="toctext">Trade</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-18"><a href="#Energy"><span class="tocnumber">5.3</span> <span class="toctext">Energy</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-19"><a href="#Transport"><span class="tocnumber">5.4</span> <span class="toctext">Transport</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-20"><a href="#Demographics"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Demographics</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-21"><a href="#Functional_urban_areas"><span class="tocnumber">6.1</span> <span class="toctext">Functional urban areas</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-22"><a href="#Languages"><span class="tocnumber">6.2</span> <span class="toctext">Languages</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-23"><a href="#Healthcare"><span class="tocnumber">6.3</span> <span class="toctext">Healthcare</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-24"><a href="#Education"><span class="tocnumber">6.4</span> <span class="toctext">Education</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-25"><a href="#Religion"><span class="tocnumber">6.5</span> <span class="toctext">Religion</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-26"><a href="#Culture"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Culture</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-27"><a href="#Literature"><span class="tocnumber">7.1</span> <span class="toctext">Literature</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-28"><a href="#Music_and_dance"><span class="tocnumber">7.2</span> <span class="toctext">Music and dance</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-29"><a href="#Architecture"><span class="tocnumber">7.3</span> <span class="toctext">Architecture</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-30"><a href="#Media"><span class="tocnumber">7.4</span> <span class="toctext">Media</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-31"><a href="#Cuisine"><span class="tocnumber">7.5</span> <span class="toctext">Cuisine</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-32"><a href="#Sports"><span class="tocnumber">7.6</span> <span class="toctext">Sports</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-33"><a href="#Society"><span class="tocnumber">7.7</span> <span class="toctext">Society</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-34"><a href="#State_symbols"><span class="tocnumber">7.8</span> <span class="toctext">State symbols</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-35"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-36"><a href="#Notes"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-37"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-38"><a href="#Bibliography"><span class="tocnumber">10.1</span> <span class="toctext">Bibliography</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-39"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-40"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Name">Name</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Names_of_the_Irish_state" title="Names of the Irish state">Names of the Irish state</a></div>\n<p>The 1922 state, comprising 26 of the 32 <a href="/wiki/Counties_of_Ireland" title="Counties of Ireland">counties of Ireland</a>, was "styled and known as the Irish Free State".<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Ireland" title="Constitution of Ireland">Constitution of Ireland</a>, adopted in 1937, provides that "the name of the State is <b>\xc3\x89ire</b>, or, in the English language, Ireland". Section 2 of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland_Act_1948" title="Republic of Ireland Act 1948">Republic of Ireland Act 1948</a> states, "It is hereby declared that the description of the State shall be the Republic of Ireland." The 1948 Act does not <i>name</i> the state as "Republic of Ireland", because to have done so would have put it in conflict with the Constitution.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The government of the United Kingdom used the name "Eire" (without the <a href="/wiki/Diacritic" title="Diacritic">diacritic</a>) and, from 1949, "Republic of Ireland", for the state;<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> it was not until the 1998 <a href="/wiki/Good_Friday_Agreement" title="Good Friday Agreement">Good Friday Agreement</a> that it used the name "Ireland".<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As well as "Ireland", "\xc3\x89ire" or "the Republic of Ireland", the state is also referred to as "the Republic", "<b>Southern Ireland</b>" or "the South".<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> In an <a href="/wiki/Irish_republican" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish republican">Irish republican</a> context it is often referred to as "the Free State" or "the 26 Counties".<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Republic_of_Ireland" title="History of the Republic of Ireland">History of the Republic of Ireland</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For the history of the entire island, see <a href="/wiki/History_of_Ireland" title="History of Ireland">History of Ireland</a>.</div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Home-rule_movement">Home-rule movement</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Home_Rule_movement" class="mw-redirect" title="Home Rule movement">Home Rule movement</a></div>\n<p>From the <a href="/wiki/Act_of_Union_1800" class="mw-redirect" title="Act of Union 1800">Act of Union</a> on 1 January 1801, until 6 December 1922, the island of Ireland was part of the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland">United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland</a>. During the <a href="/wiki/Great_Famine_(Ireland)" title="Great Famine (Ireland)">Great Famine</a>, from 1845 to 1849, the island\'s population of over 8 million fell by 30%. One million Irish died of starvation and/or disease and another 1.5 million emigrated, mostly to the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> This set the pattern of emigration for the century to come, resulting in constant population decline up to the 1960s.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Charles_Stewart_Parnell_-_Brady-Handy.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Charles_Stewart_Parnell_-_Brady-Handy.jpg/170px-Charles_Stewart_Parnell_-_Brady-Handy.jpg" width="170" height="213" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Charles_Stewart_Parnell_-_Brady-Handy.jpg/255px-Charles_Stewart_Parnell_-_Brady-Handy.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Charles_Stewart_Parnell_-_Brady-Handy.jpg/340px-Charles_Stewart_Parnell_-_Brady-Handy.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3232" data-file-height="4059" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Charles_Stewart_Parnell_-_Brady-Handy.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Irish_Parliamentary_Party" title="Irish Parliamentary Party">Irish Parliamentary Party</a> was formed in 1882 by <a href="/wiki/Charles_Stewart_Parnell" title="Charles Stewart Parnell">Charles Stewart Parnell</a> (1846\xe2\x80\x931891).</div></div></div>\n<p>From 1874, and particularly under <a href="/wiki/Charles_Stewart_Parnell" title="Charles Stewart Parnell">Charles Stewart Parnell</a> from 1880, the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Parliamentary_Party" title="Irish Parliamentary Party">Irish Parliamentary Party</a> gained prominence. This was firstly through widespread agrarian agitation via the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Land_League" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish Land League">Irish Land League</a>, that won <a href="/wiki/Land_reforms" class="mw-redirect" title="Land reforms">land reforms</a> for tenants in the form of the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Land_Acts" title="Irish Land Acts">Irish Land Acts</a>, and secondly through its attempts to achieve <a href="/wiki/Irish_Home_Rule_Movement" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish Home Rule Movement">Home Rule</a>, via two unsuccessful bills which would have granted Ireland limited national autonomy. These led to "grass-roots" control of national affairs, under the <a href="/wiki/Local_Government_(Ireland)_Act_1898" title="Local Government (Ireland) Act 1898">Local Government Act 1898</a>, that had been in the hands of landlord-dominated <a href="/wiki/Grand_juries" class="mw-redirect" title="Grand juries">grand juries</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Protestant_Ascendancy" title="Protestant Ascendancy">Protestant Ascendancy</a>.\n</p><p>Home Rule seemed certain when the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_Act_1911" title="Parliament Act 1911">Parliament Act 1911</a> abolished the veto of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Lords" title="House of Lords">House of Lords</a>, and <a href="/wiki/John_Redmond" title="John Redmond">John Redmond</a> secured the <a href="/wiki/Home_Rule_Act_1914" class="mw-redirect" title="Home Rule Act 1914">Third Home Rule Act</a> in 1914. However, the <a href="/wiki/Unionism_in_Ireland" title="Unionism in Ireland">Unionist movement</a> had been growing since 1886 among Irish Protestants after the introduction of the first home rule bill, fearing discrimination and loss of economic and social privileges if <a href="/wiki/Irish_Catholics" title="Irish Catholics">Irish Catholics</a> achieved real political power. In the late 19th and early 20th century unionism was particularly strong in parts of <a href="/wiki/Ulster" title="Ulster">Ulster</a>, where industrialisation was more common in contrast to the more agrarian rest of the island, and where the Protestant population was more prominent, with a majority in four counties.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Under the leadership of the Dublin-born <a href="/wiki/Edward_Carson,_Baron_Carson" class="mw-redirect" title="Edward Carson, Baron Carson">Sir Edward Carson</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Unionist_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish Unionist Party">Irish Unionist Party</a> and the Ulsterman <a href="/wiki/James_Craig,_1st_Viscount_Craigavon" title="James Craig, 1st Viscount Craigavon">Sir James Craig</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Ulster_Unionist_Party" title="Ulster Unionist Party">Ulster Unionist Party</a>, unionists became <a href="/wiki/Ulster_Volunteers" title="Ulster Volunteers">strongly militant</a> in order to oppose "the Coercion of Ulster".<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> After the Home Rule Bill passed parliament in May 1914, to avoid rebellion with Ulster, the British Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/H._H._Asquith" title="H. H. Asquith">H. H. Asquith</a> introduced an <a href="/wiki/Irish_Parliamentary_Party#Home_Rule_succeeds" title="Irish Parliamentary Party">Amending Bill</a> reluctantly conceded to by the Irish Party leadership. This provided for the temporary exclusion of Ulster from the workings of the bill for a trial period of six years, with an as yet undecided new set of measures to be introduced for the area to be temporarily excluded.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Revolution_and_steps_to_independence">Revolution and steps to independence</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Easter_Proclamation_of_1916.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Easter_Proclamation_of_1916.png/170px-Easter_Proclamation_of_1916.png" width="170" height="258" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Easter_Proclamation_of_1916.png/255px-Easter_Proclamation_of_1916.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Easter_Proclamation_of_1916.png/340px-Easter_Proclamation_of_1916.png 2x" data-file-width="954" data-file-height="1450" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Easter_Proclamation_of_1916.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Proclamation_of_the_Irish_Republic" title="Proclamation of the Irish Republic">Easter Proclamation</a>, 1916</div></div></div>\n<p>Though it received the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Assent" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal Assent">Royal Assent</a> and was placed on the statute books in 1914, the implementation of the <a href="/wiki/Home_Rule_Act_1914" class="mw-redirect" title="Home Rule Act 1914">Third Home Rule Act</a> was suspended until after the <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">First World War</a> which defused the threat of civil war in Ireland. With the hope of ensuring the implementation of the Act at the end of the war through <a href="/wiki/Ireland_and_World_War_I" title="Ireland and World War I">Ireland\'s engagement in the war</a>, Redmond and his Irish <a href="/wiki/National_Volunteers" title="National Volunteers">National Volunteers</a> supported Britain and its <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_I" title="Allies of World War I">Allies</a>. 175,000 men joined <a href="/wiki/Irish_regiment" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish regiment">Irish regiments</a> of the <a href="/wiki/10th_(Irish)_Division_(United_Kingdom)" class="mw-redirect" title="10th (Irish) Division (United Kingdom)">10th (Irish)</a> and <a href="/wiki/16th_(Irish)_Division_(United_Kingdom)" class="mw-redirect" title="16th (Irish) Division (United Kingdom)">16th (Irish)</a> divisions of the <a href="/wiki/Kitchener%27s_Army" title="Kitchener&#39;s Army">New British Army</a>, while Unionists joined the <a href="/wiki/36th_(Ulster)_Division" title="36th (Ulster) Division">36th (Ulster)</a> divisions.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The remainder of the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Volunteers" title="Irish Volunteers">Irish Volunteers</a>, who opposed any support of Britain, launched an armed insurrection against British rule in the 1916 <a href="/wiki/Easter_Rising" title="Easter Rising">Easter Rising</a>, together with the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Citizen_Army" title="Irish Citizen Army">Irish Citizen Army</a>. This commenced on 24 April 1916 with the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Declaration_of_Independence" title="Irish Declaration of Independence">declaration of independence</a>. After a week of heavy fighting, primarily in Dublin, the surviving rebels were forced to surrender their positions. The majority were imprisoned but fifteen of the prisoners (including most of the leaders) were executed as traitors to Britain. This included <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Pearse" title="Patrick Pearse">Patrick Pearse</a>, the spokesman for the rising and who provided the signal to the volunteers to start the rising, as well as <a href="/wiki/James_Connolly" title="James Connolly">James Connolly</a>, socialist and founder of the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Workers_of_the_World" title="Industrial Workers of the World">Industrial Workers of the World</a> union and both the Irish and Scottish Labour movements. These events, together with the <a href="/wiki/Conscription_Crisis_of_1918" title="Conscription Crisis of 1918">Conscription Crisis of 1918</a>, had a profound effect on changing public opinion in Ireland.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In January 1919, after the December <a href="/wiki/Irish_general_election,_1918" title="Irish general election, 1918">1918 general election</a>, 73 of Ireland\'s 106 <a href="/wiki/Member_of_Parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Member of Parliament">Members of Parliament</a> (MPs) elected were <a href="/wiki/History_of_Sinn_F%C3%A9in" title="History of Sinn F\xc3\xa9in">Sinn F\xc3\xa9in</a> members who refused to take their seats in the <a href="/wiki/British_House_of_Commons" class="mw-redirect" title="British House of Commons">British House of Commons</a>. Instead, they set up an Irish parliament called <a href="/wiki/D%C3%A1il_%C3%89ireann_(Irish_Republic)" title="D\xc3\xa1il \xc3\x89ireann (Irish Republic)">D\xc3\xa1il \xc3\x89ireann</a>. This <a href="/wiki/First_D%C3%A1il" title="First D\xc3\xa1il">first D\xc3\xa1il</a> in January 1919 issued a <a href="/wiki/Declaration_of_independence" title="Declaration of independence">Declaration of Independence</a> and proclaimed an <a href="/wiki/Irish_Republic" title="Irish Republic">Irish Republic</a>. The Declaration was mainly a restatement of the <a href="/wiki/Proclamation_of_the_Irish_Republic" title="Proclamation of the Irish Republic">1916 Proclamation</a> with the additional provision that Ireland was no longer a part of the United Kingdom. The new Irish Republic was recognised internationally only by the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Soviet_Federative_Socialist_Republic" title="Russian Soviet Federative Socialist Republic">Russian Soviet Republic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> The Irish Republic\'s <i><i lang="ga" title="Irish language text"><a href="/wiki/Aireacht" class="mw-redirect" title="Aireacht">Aireacht</a></i></i> (Ministry) sent a delegation under <i><i lang="ga" title="Irish language text"><a href="/wiki/Ceann_Comhairle" title="Ceann Comhairle">Ceann Comhairle</a></i></i> (Head of Council, or Speaker, of the Da\xc3\xadl) <a href="/wiki/Se%C3%A1n_T._O%27Kelly" title="Se\xc3\xa1n T. O&#39;Kelly">Se\xc3\xa1n T. O\'Kelly</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Paris_Peace_Conference,_1919" title="Paris Peace Conference, 1919">Paris Peace Conference</a> of 1919, but it was not admitted.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:D%C3%A1il_Chamber.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/D%C3%A1il_Chamber.jpg/220px-D%C3%A1il_Chamber.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/D%C3%A1il_Chamber.jpg/330px-D%C3%A1il_Chamber.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/D%C3%A1il_Chamber.jpg/440px-D%C3%A1il_Chamber.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="533" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:D%C3%A1il_Chamber.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>In 1922 a new parliament called the <a href="/wiki/Oireachtas_of_the_Irish_Free_State" title="Oireachtas of the Irish Free State">Oireachtas</a> was established, of which <a href="/wiki/D%C3%A1il_%C3%89ireann" title="D\xc3\xa1il \xc3\x89ireann">D\xc3\xa1il \xc3\x89ireann</a> became the <a href="/wiki/Lower_house" title="Lower house">lower house</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>After the <a href="/wiki/Irish_War_of_Independence" title="Irish War of Independence">War of Independence</a> and truce called in July 1921, representatives of the <a href="/wiki/British_government" class="mw-redirect" title="British government">British government</a> and the Irish treaty delegates, led by <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Griffith" title="Arthur Griffith">Arthur Griffith</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Barton" title="Robert Barton">Robert Barton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Michael_Collins_(Irish_leader)" title="Michael Collins (Irish leader)">Michael Collins</a>, negotiated the Anglo-Irish Treaty in London from 11 October to 6 December 1921. The Irish delegates set up headquarters at <a href="/wiki/Hans_Place" title="Hans Place">Hans Place</a> in <a href="/wiki/Knightsbridge" title="Knightsbridge">Knightsbridge</a>, and it was here in private discussions that the decision was taken on 5 December to recommend the treaty to D\xc3\xa1il \xc3\x89ireann.\nThe <a href="/wiki/Second_D%C3%A1il" title="Second D\xc3\xa1il">Second D\xc3\xa1il \xc3\x89ireann</a> <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Irish_Treaty_D%C3%A1il_vote" title="Anglo-Irish Treaty D\xc3\xa1il vote">narrowly ratified</a> the Treaty.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In accordance with the treaty, on 6 December 1922 the entire island of Ireland became a self-governing <a href="/wiki/Dominion" title="Dominion">Dominion</a> called the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Free_State" title="Irish Free State">Irish Free State</a> (<i>Saorst\xc3\xa1t \xc3\x89ireann</i>). Under the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_the_Irish_Free_State" title="Constitution of the Irish Free State">Constitution of the Irish Free State</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Northern_Ireland" title="Parliament of Northern Ireland">Parliament of Northern Ireland</a> had the option to leave the Irish Free State one month later and return to the United Kingdom. During the intervening period, the powers of the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_Irish_Free_State" class="mw-redirect" title="Parliament of the Irish Free State">Parliament of the Irish Free State</a> and <a href="/wiki/Executive_Council_of_the_Irish_Free_State" title="Executive Council of the Irish Free State">Executive Council of the Irish Free State</a> did not extend to Northern Ireland. Northern Ireland exercised its right under the treaty to leave the new Dominion and rejoined the United Kingdom on 8 December 1922. It did so by making an address to the King requesting, "that the powers of the Parliament and Government of the Irish Free State shall no longer extend to Northern Ireland."<sup id="cite_ref-ahds1922_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ahds1922-33">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> The Irish Free State was a <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a> sharing a monarch with the United Kingdom and other Dominions of the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">British Commonwealth</a>. The country had a <a href="/wiki/Governor-General_of_the_Irish_Free_State" title="Governor-General of the Irish Free State">governor-general</a> (representing the monarch), a <a href="/wiki/Bicameralism" title="Bicameralism">bicameral</a> parliament, a cabinet called the "Executive Council", and a prime minister called the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Executive_Council_of_the_Irish_Free_State" title="President of the Executive Council of the Irish Free State">President of the Executive Council</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Irish_Civil_War">Irish Civil War</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eamon_de_Valera_(7038732625).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Eamon_de_Valera_%287038732625%29.jpg/170px-Eamon_de_Valera_%287038732625%29.jpg" width="170" height="221" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Eamon_de_Valera_%287038732625%29.jpg/255px-Eamon_de_Valera_%287038732625%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Eamon_de_Valera_%287038732625%29.jpg/340px-Eamon_de_Valera_%287038732625%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1919" data-file-height="2500" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eamon_de_Valera_(7038732625).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/%C3%89amon_de_Valera" title="\xc3\x89amon de Valera">\xc3\x89amon de Valera</a> (1882\xe2\x80\x931975)</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Irish_Civil_War" title="Irish Civil War">Irish Civil War</a> (June 1922 \xe2\x80\x93 May 1923) was the consequence of the creation of the Irish Free State. Anti-treaty forces, led by <a href="/wiki/%C3%89amon_de_Valera" title="\xc3\x89amon de Valera">\xc3\x89amon de Valera</a>, objected to the fact that acceptance of the treaty <i>abolished</i> the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Republic" title="Irish Republic">Irish Republic</a> of 1919 to which they had sworn loyalty, arguing in the face of public support for the settlement that the "people have no right to do wrong".<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> They objected most to the fact that the state would remain part of the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a> and that members of the <a href="/wiki/Oireachtas_of_the_Irish_Free_State" title="Oireachtas of the Irish Free State">Free State Parliament</a> would have to swear what the Anti-treaty side saw as an oath of fidelity to the British King. Pro-treaty forces, led by <a href="/wiki/Michael_Collins_(Irish_leader)" title="Michael Collins (Irish leader)">Michael Collins</a>, argued that the treaty gave "not the ultimate freedom that all nations aspire to and develop, but the freedom to achieve it".<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>At the start of the war, the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Republican_Army_(1917%E2%80%9322)" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish Republican Army (1917\xe2\x80\x9322)">Irish Republican Army</a> (IRA) split into two opposing camps: a pro-treaty IRA and an <a href="/wiki/Irish_Republican_Army_(1922%E2%80%931969)" title="Irish Republican Army (1922\xe2\x80\x931969)">anti-treaty IRA</a>. The pro-treaty IRA disbanded and joined the new <a href="/wiki/National_Army_(Ireland)" title="National Army (Ireland)">National Army</a>. However, because the anti-treaty IRA lacked an effective command structure and because of the pro-treaty forces\' defensive tactics throughout the war, Michael Collins and his pro-treaty forces were able to build up an army with many tens of thousands of World War I veterans from the 1922 disbanded <a href="/wiki/Irish_regiments#Irish_regiments_of_the_British_Army" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish regiments">Irish regiments</a> of the British Army, capable of overwhelming the anti-treatyists. British supplies of artillery, aircraft, machine-guns and ammunition boosted pro-treaty forces, and the threat of a return of Crown forces to the Free State removed any doubts about the necessity of enforcing the treaty. The lack of public support for the anti-treaty forces (often called the <i>Irregulars</i>) and the determination of the government to overcome the Irregulars contributed significantly to their defeat.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Constitution_of_Ireland_1937">Constitution of Ireland 1937</span></h3>\n<p>Following a national plebiscite in July 1937, the new <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Ireland" title="Constitution of Ireland">Constitution of Ireland</a> (<i>Bunreacht na h\xc3\x89ireann</i>) <a href="/wiki/Adoption_of_the_Constitution_of_Ireland" title="Adoption of the Constitution of Ireland">came into force</a> on 29 December 1937.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> This replaced the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_the_Irish_Free_State" title="Constitution of the Irish Free State">Constitution of the Irish Free State</a> and called the state <i>Ireland</i>, or <i>\xc3\x89ire</i> in Irish.<sup id="cite_ref-1937rename_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1937rename-37">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> While <a href="/wiki/Articles_2_and_3_of_the_Constitution_of_Ireland" title="Articles 2 and 3 of the Constitution of Ireland">Articles 2 and 3</a> of the Constitution defined the national territory to be the whole island, they also confined the state\'s jurisdiction to the area that had been the Irish Free State. The former Irish Free State government had abolished the Office of <a href="/wiki/Governor-General_of_the_Irish_Free_State" title="Governor-General of the Irish Free State">Governor-General</a> in December 1936. Although the constitution established the office of <a href="/wiki/President_of_Ireland" title="President of Ireland">President of Ireland</a>, the question over whether Ireland was a republic remained open. Diplomats were accredited to the king, but the president exercised all internal functions of a head of state.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> For instance, the President gave assent to new laws with his own authority, without reference to <a href="/wiki/King_George_VI" class="mw-redirect" title="King George VI">King George VI</a> who was only an "organ", that was provided for by statute law.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Irish_neutrality_during_World_War_II" title="Irish neutrality during World War II">Ireland remained neutral</a> during World War II, a period it described as the <a href="/wiki/The_Emergency_(Ireland)" title="The Emergency (Ireland)">Emergency</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Ireland\'s link with the Commonwealth was terminated with the passage of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland_Act_1948" title="Republic of Ireland Act 1948">Republic of Ireland Act 1948</a>, which came into force on 18 April 1949 and declared that the state was a republic. At the time, a declaration of a republic terminated Commonwealth membership. This rule was changed 10 days after Ireland declared itself a republic, with the <a href="/wiki/London_Declaration" title="London Declaration">London Declaration</a> of 28 April 1949. Ireland did not reapply when the rules were altered to permit republics to join. Later, the Crown of Ireland Act was repealed in Ireland by the Statute Law Revision (Pre-Union Irish Statutes) Act 1962.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recent_history">Recent history</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_(081).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg/220px-Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg" width="220" height="131" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg/330px-Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg/440px-Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="521" data-file-height="310" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_(081).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>In 1973 Ireland joined the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Community" title="European Economic Community">European Economic Community</a> along with the United Kingdom and Denmark. The country signed the <a href="/wiki/Lisbon_Treaty" class="mw-redirect" title="Lisbon Treaty">Lisbon Treaty</a> in 2007.</div></div></div>\n<p>Ireland became a member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> in December 1955, after having been denied membership because of its <a href="/wiki/Irish_neutrality_during_World_War_II" title="Irish neutrality during World War II">neutral stance</a> during the Second World War and not supporting the <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Allied cause</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> At the time, joining the UN involved a commitment to using force to deter aggression by one state against another if the UN thought it was necessary.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Interest towards membership of the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Community" title="European Economic Community">European Economic Community</a> (EEC) developed in Ireland during the 1950s, with consideration also given to membership of the <a href="/wiki/European_Free_Trade_Area" class="mw-redirect" title="European Free Trade Area">European Free Trade Area</a>. As the United Kingdom intended on EEC membership, Ireland applied for membership in July 1961 due to the substantial economic linkages with the United Kingdom. However, the founding EEC members remained skeptical regarding Ireland\'s economic capacity, neutrality, and unattractive <a href="/wiki/Protectionist" class="mw-redirect" title="Protectionist">protectionist</a> policy.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> Many Irish economists and politicians realised that economic policy reform was necessary. The prospect of EEC membership became doubtful in 1963 when French President General <a href="/wiki/Charles_de_Gaulle" title="Charles de Gaulle">Charles de Gaulle</a> stated that France opposed Britain\'s accession, which ceased negotiations with all other candidate countries. However, in 1969 his successor, <a href="/wiki/Georges_Pompidou" title="Georges Pompidou">Georges Pompidou</a>, was not opposed to British and Irish membership. Negotiations began and in 1972 the Treaty of Accession was signed. A <a href="/wiki/Third_Amendment_of_the_Constitution_of_Ireland" title="Third Amendment of the Constitution of Ireland">referendum held in 1972</a> confirmed Ireland\'s entry, and it finally joined the EEC in 1973.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The economic crisis of the late 1970s was fuelled by the <a href="/wiki/Fianna_F%C3%A1il" title="Fianna F\xc3\xa1il">Fianna F\xc3\xa1il</a> government\'s budget, the abolition of the car tax, excessive borrowing, and global economic instability including the <a href="/wiki/1979_oil_crisis" title="1979 oil crisis">1979 oil crisis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-tcdtax_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tcdtax-45">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> There were significant policy changes from 1989 onwards, with economic reform, tax cuts, welfare reform, an increase in competition, and a ban on borrowing to fund current spending. This policy began in 1989\xe2\x80\x931992 by the Fianna F\xc3\xa1il/<a href="/wiki/Progressive_Democrats" title="Progressive Democrats">Progressive Democrat</a> government, and continued by the subsequent Fianna F\xc3\xa1il/<a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(Ireland)" title="Labour Party (Ireland)">Labour</a> government and <a href="/wiki/Fine_Gael" title="Fine Gael">Fine Gael</a>/Labour/<a href="/wiki/Democratic_Left_(Ireland)" title="Democratic Left (Ireland)">Democratic Left</a> government. Ireland became one of the world\'s fastest growing economies by the late 1990s in what was known as the <a href="/wiki/Celtic_Tiger" title="Celtic Tiger">Celtic Tiger</a> period, which lasted until the global <a href="/wiki/Financial_crisis_of_2007%E2%80%9308" class="mw-redirect" title="Financial crisis of 2007\xe2\x80\x9308">Financial crisis of 2007\xe2\x80\x9308</a>. However, since 2014, Ireland has experienced increased economic activity.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the Northern Ireland question, the British and Irish governments started to seek a peaceful resolution to the violent conflict involving many <a href="/wiki/Paramilitary" title="Paramilitary">paramilitaries</a> and the <a href="/wiki/British_Army" title="British Army">British Army</a> in Northern Ireland known as "<a href="/wiki/The_Troubles" title="The Troubles">The Troubles</a>". A peace settlement for Northern Ireland, known as the <a href="/wiki/Good_Friday_Agreement" title="Good Friday Agreement">Good Friday Agreement</a>, was approved in 1998 in referendums north and south of the border. As part of the peace settlement, the territorial claim to Northern Ireland in <a href="/wiki/Articles_2_and_3_of_the_Constitution_of_Ireland" title="Articles 2 and 3 of the Constitution of Ireland">Articles 2 and 3 of the Constitution of Ireland</a> was removed by referendum. In its white paper on <a href="/wiki/Brexit" title="Brexit">Brexit</a> the United Kingdom government reiterated its commitment to the Good Friday Agreement. With regard to Northern Ireland\'s status, it said that the UK Government\'s "clearly-stated preference is to retain Northern Ireland\xe2\x80\x99s current constitutional position: as part of the UK, but with strong links to Ireland".<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Ireland" title="Geography of Ireland">Geography of Ireland</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cliffs_of_Moher_bei_bestem_Wetter_(2007).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Cliffs_of_Moher_bei_bestem_Wetter_%282007%29.jpg/220px-Cliffs_of_Moher_bei_bestem_Wetter_%282007%29.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Cliffs_of_Moher_bei_bestem_Wetter_%282007%29.jpg/330px-Cliffs_of_Moher_bei_bestem_Wetter_%282007%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Cliffs_of_Moher_bei_bestem_Wetter_%282007%29.jpg/440px-Cliffs_of_Moher_bei_bestem_Wetter_%282007%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2100" data-file-height="1575" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cliffs_of_Moher_bei_bestem_Wetter_(2007).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Cliffs_of_Moher" title="Cliffs of Moher">Cliffs of Moher</a> on the Atlantic coast</div></div></div>\n<p>The state extends over an area of about five-sixths (70,273&#160;km<sup>2</sup> or 27,133&#160;sq&#160;mi) of the island of <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a> (84,421&#160;km<sup>2</sup> or 32,595&#160;sq&#160;mi), with <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a> constituting the remainder. The island is bounded to the north and west by the Atlantic Ocean and to the northeast by the <a href="/wiki/North_Channel_(Great_Britain_and_Ireland)" title="North Channel (Great Britain and Ireland)">North Channel</a>. To the east, the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Sea" title="Irish Sea">Irish Sea</a> connects to the Atlantic Ocean via <a href="/wiki/St_George%27s_Channel" title="St George&#39;s Channel">St George\'s Channel</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Celtic_Sea" title="Celtic Sea">Celtic Sea</a> to the southwest.\n</p><p>The western landscape mostly consists of rugged cliffs, hills and mountains. The central lowlands are extensively covered with glacial deposits of clay and sand, as well as significant areas of <a href="/wiki/Bogland" class="mw-redirect" title="Bogland">bogland</a> and several lakes. The highest point is <a href="/wiki/Carrauntoohil" title="Carrauntoohil">Carrauntoohil</a> (1,038&#160;m or 3,406&#160;ft), located in the <a href="/wiki/Macgillycuddy%27s_Reeks" title="Macgillycuddy&#39;s Reeks">Macgillycuddy\'s Reeks</a> mountain range in the southwest. <a href="/wiki/River_Shannon" title="River Shannon">River Shannon</a>, which traverses the central lowlands, is the longest river in Ireland at 386 kilometres or 240 miles in length. The west coast is more rugged than the east, with numerous islands, <a href="/wiki/Peninsula" title="Peninsula">peninsulas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Headland" title="Headland">headlands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bay" title="Bay">bays</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Macgillycuddy%27s_Reeks,_Lough_Callee_and_Cnoc_na_P%C3%A9iste_(Knocknapeasta)_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1434579.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Macgillycuddy%27s_Reeks%2C_Lough_Callee_and_Cnoc_na_P%C3%A9iste_%28Knocknapeasta%29_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1434579.jpg/220px-Macgillycuddy%27s_Reeks%2C_Lough_Callee_and_Cnoc_na_P%C3%A9iste_%28Knocknapeasta%29_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1434579.jpg" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Macgillycuddy%27s_Reeks%2C_Lough_Callee_and_Cnoc_na_P%C3%A9iste_%28Knocknapeasta%29_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1434579.jpg/330px-Macgillycuddy%27s_Reeks%2C_Lough_Callee_and_Cnoc_na_P%C3%A9iste_%28Knocknapeasta%29_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1434579.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Macgillycuddy%27s_Reeks%2C_Lough_Callee_and_Cnoc_na_P%C3%A9iste_%28Knocknapeasta%29_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1434579.jpg/440px-Macgillycuddy%27s_Reeks%2C_Lough_Callee_and_Cnoc_na_P%C3%A9iste_%28Knocknapeasta%29_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1434579.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="420" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Macgillycuddy%27s_Reeks,_Lough_Callee_and_Cnoc_na_P%C3%A9iste_(Knocknapeasta)_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1434579.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Macgillycuddy%27s_Reeks" title="Macgillycuddy&#39;s Reeks">Macgillycuddy\'s Reeks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mountain_range" title="Mountain range">mountain range</a> in <a href="/wiki/County_Kerry" title="County Kerry">County Kerry</a> includes the highest peaks in Ireland</div></div></div>\n<p>Before the arrival of the first settlers in Ireland about 9,000 years ago, the land was largely covered by forests of <a href="/wiki/Oak" title="Oak">oak</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fraxinus_excelsior" title="Fraxinus excelsior">ash</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elm" title="Elm">elm</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hazel" title="Hazel">hazel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taxus_baccata" title="Taxus baccata">yew</a>, and other native trees.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> The growth of <a href="/wiki/Blanket_bog" title="Blanket bog">blanket bog</a> and the extensive clearing of woodland to facilitate farming are believed to be the main causes of <a href="/wiki/Deforestation" title="Deforestation">deforestation</a> during the following centuries. Today, about 12% of Ireland is forested, of which a significant majority is composed of mainly non-native <a href="/wiki/Coniferous" class="mw-redirect" title="Coniferous">coniferous</a> plantations for commercial use.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> Ideal soil conditions, high rainfall and a mild climate give Ireland the highest growth rates for forests in Europe. <a href="/wiki/Hedgerows" class="mw-redirect" title="Hedgerows">Hedgerows</a>, which are traditionally used to define land boundaries, are an important substitute for woodland habitat, providing refuge for native wild flora and a wide range of insect, bird and mammal species.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Glendalough.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Glendalough.jpg/220px-Glendalough.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Glendalough.jpg/330px-Glendalough.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Glendalough.jpg/440px-Glendalough.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1920" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Glendalough.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Glendalough" title="Glendalough">Glendalough</a> valley in <a href="/wiki/County_Wicklow" title="County Wicklow">County Wicklow</a></div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">Agriculture</a> accounts for about 64% of the total land area.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> This has resulted in limited land to preserve natural habitats, in particular for larger wild mammals with greater territorial requirements.<sup id="cite_ref-land_cover_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-land_cover-52">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> The long history of agricultural production coupled with modern agricultural methods, such as <a href="/wiki/Pesticide" title="Pesticide">pesticide</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fertiliser" class="mw-redirect" title="Fertiliser">fertiliser</a> use, has placed pressure on <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">biodiversity</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-53">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Ireland" title="Climate of Ireland">Climate of Ireland</a></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a> and the warming influence of the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Stream" title="Gulf Stream">Gulf Stream</a> affect weather patterns in Ireland.<sup id="cite_ref-climate_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-climate-54">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> Temperatures differ regionally, with central and eastern areas tending to be more extreme. However, due to a <a href="/wiki/Temperate_climate" title="Temperate climate">temperate</a> <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">oceanic climate</a>, temperatures are seldom lower than \xe2\x88\x925&#160;\xc2\xb0C (23&#160;\xc2\xb0F) in winter or higher than 26&#160;\xc2\xb0C (79&#160;\xc2\xb0F) in summer.<sup id="cite_ref-irishclimate_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-irishclimate-55">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> The highest temperature recorded in Ireland was 33.3&#160;\xc2\xb0C (91.9&#160;\xc2\xb0F) on 26 June 1887 at <a href="/wiki/Kilkenny_Castle" title="Kilkenny Castle">Kilkenny Castle</a> in Kilkenny, while the lowest temperature recorded was \xe2\x88\x9219.1&#160;\xc2\xb0C (\xe2\x88\x922.4&#160;\xc2\xb0F) at <a href="/wiki/Markree_Castle" title="Markree Castle">Markree Castle</a> in Sligo.<sup id="cite_ref-metie_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-metie-56">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> Rainfall is more prevalent during winter months and less so during the early months of summer. Southwestern areas experience the most rainfall as a result of south westerly winds, while <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin</a> receives the least. Sunshine duration is highest in the southeast of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-climate_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-climate-54">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> The far north and west are two of the windiest regions in Europe, with great potential for <a href="/wiki/Wind_energy" class="mw-redirect" title="Wind energy">wind energy</a> generation.<sup id="cite_ref-winds_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-winds-57">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>\nIreland normally gets between 1100 and 1600 hours of sunshine each year, most areas averaging between 3.25 and 3.75 hours a day. The sunniest months are May and June, which average between 5 and 6.5 hours per day over most of the country. The extreme southeast gets most sunshine, averaging over 7 hours a day in early summer. December is the dullest month, with an average daily sunshine ranging from about 1 hour in the north to almost 2 hours in the extreme southeast. The sunniest summer in the 100 years from 1881 to 1980 was 1887, according to measurements made at the Phoenix Park in Dublin; 1980 was the dullest.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_the_Republic_of_Ireland" title="Politics of the Republic of Ireland">Politics of the Republic of Ireland</a></div>\n<p>Ireland is a constitutional republic with a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">parliamentary system</a> of government. The <i><i lang="ga" title="Irish language text"><a href="/wiki/Oireachtas" title="Oireachtas">Oireachtas</a></i></i> is the <a href="/wiki/Bicameral" class="mw-redirect" title="Bicameral">bicameral</a> national parliament composed of the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Ireland" title="President of Ireland">President of Ireland</a> and the two Houses of the Oireachtas:\n<i><i lang="ga" title="Irish language text"><a href="/wiki/Seanad_%C3%89ireann" title="Seanad \xc3\x89ireann">Seanad \xc3\x89ireann</a></i></i> (Senate) and <i><i lang="ga" title="Irish language text"><a href="/wiki/D%C3%A1il_%C3%89ireann" title="D\xc3\xa1il \xc3\x89ireann">D\xc3\xa1il \xc3\x89ireann</a></i></i> (House of Representatives).<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/%C3%81ras_an_Uachtar%C3%A1in" title="\xc3\x81ras an Uachtar\xc3\xa1in">\xc3\x81ras an Uachtar\xc3\xa1in</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Official_residence" title="Official residence">official residence</a> of the President of Ireland, while the houses of the Oireachtas meet at <a href="/wiki/Leinster_House" title="Leinster House">Leinster House</a> in <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:President_Higgins%27s_visit_FINIRISH_BATT_HQ,_Lebanon_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/President_Higgins%27s_visit_FINIRISH_BATT_HQ%2C_Lebanon_%28cropped%29.jpg/170px-President_Higgins%27s_visit_FINIRISH_BATT_HQ%2C_Lebanon_%28cropped%29.jpg" width="170" height="208" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/President_Higgins%27s_visit_FINIRISH_BATT_HQ%2C_Lebanon_%28cropped%29.jpg/255px-President_Higgins%27s_visit_FINIRISH_BATT_HQ%2C_Lebanon_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/President_Higgins%27s_visit_FINIRISH_BATT_HQ%2C_Lebanon_%28cropped%29.jpg/340px-President_Higgins%27s_visit_FINIRISH_BATT_HQ%2C_Lebanon_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1530" data-file-height="1869" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:President_Higgins%27s_visit_FINIRISH_BATT_HQ,_Lebanon_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>President <a href="/wiki/Michael_D._Higgins" title="Michael D. Higgins">Michael D. Higgins</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The President serves as <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a>, and is elected for a seven-year term and may be re-elected once. The President is primarily a <a href="/wiki/Figurehead_(metaphor)" class="mw-redirect" title="Figurehead (metaphor)">figurehead</a>, but is entrusted with certain constitutional powers with the advice of the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_State_(Ireland)" title="Council of State (Ireland)">Council of State</a>. The office has absolute discretion in some areas, such as referring a bill to the Supreme Court for a judgment on its constitutionality.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Michael_D._Higgins" title="Michael D. Higgins">Michael D. Higgins</a> became the ninth President of Ireland on 11 November 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <i><i lang="ga" title="Irish language text"><a href="/wiki/Taoiseach" title="Taoiseach">Taoiseach</a></i></i> (Prime Minister) serves as the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a> and is appointed by the President upon the nomination of the <i lang="ga" title="Irish language text">D\xc3\xa1il</i>. Most <i><i lang="ga" title="Irish language text">Taoisigh</i></i> have served as the leader of the political party that gains the most seats in national elections. It has become customary for <a href="/wiki/Coalition_government" title="Coalition government">coalitions</a> to form a government, as there has not been a single-party government since 1989.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Leo_Varadkar" title="Leo Varadkar">Leo Varadkar</a> succeeded <a href="/wiki/Enda_Kenny" title="Enda Kenny">Enda Kenny</a> as Taoiseach on 14 June 2017.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Leo_Varadkar_2011.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Leo_Varadkar_2011.jpg/170px-Leo_Varadkar_2011.jpg" width="170" height="303" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Leo_Varadkar_2011.jpg/255px-Leo_Varadkar_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Leo_Varadkar_2011.jpg/340px-Leo_Varadkar_2011.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2576" data-file-height="4592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Leo_Varadkar_2011.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Taoiseach <a href="/wiki/Leo_Varadkar" title="Leo Varadkar">Leo Varadkar</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The <i lang="ga" title="Irish language text">Seanad</i> is composed of sixty members, with eleven nominated by the <i lang="ga" title="Irish language text">Taoiseach</i>, six elected by two universities, and 43 elected by public representatives from panels of candidates established on a vocational basis. The <i lang="ga" title="Irish language text">D\xc3\xa1il</i> has 158 members (<i><i lang="ga" title="Irish language text"><a href="/wiki/Teachta_D%C3%A1la" title="Teachta D\xc3\xa1la">Teachta\xc3\xad D\xc3\xa1la</a></i></i>) elected to represent multi-seat <a href="/wiki/D%C3%A1il_constituencies" title="D\xc3\xa1il constituencies">constituencies</a> under the system of <a href="/wiki/Proportional_representation" title="Proportional representation">proportional representation</a> and by means of the <a href="/wiki/Single_transferable_vote" title="Single transferable vote">single transferable vote</a>.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Ireland" title="Government of Ireland">Government</a> is constitutionally limited to fifteen members. No more than two members can be selected from the <i lang="ga" title="Irish language text">Seanad</i>, and the <i lang="ga" title="Irish language text">Taoiseach</i>, <i><i lang="ga" title="Irish language text"><a href="/wiki/T%C3%A1naiste" title="T\xc3\xa1naiste">T\xc3\xa1naiste</a></i></i> (Deputy Prime Minister) and <a href="/wiki/Minister_for_Finance_(Ireland)" title="Minister for Finance (Ireland)">Minister for Finance</a> must be members of the <i lang="ga" title="Irish language text">D\xc3\xa1il</i>. The D\xc3\xa1il must be dissolved within five years after its first meeting following the previous election,<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> and a general election for members of the D\xc3\xa1il must take place no later than thirty days after the dissolution. According to the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Ireland" title="Constitution of Ireland">Constitution of Ireland</a>, parliamentary elections must be held at least every seven years, though a lower limit may be set by statute law. The current government is a Fine Gael led minority government led by <a href="/wiki/Leo_Varadkar" title="Leo Varadkar">Leo Varadkar</a> as <a href="/wiki/Taoiseach" title="Taoiseach">Taoiseach</a> and <a href="/wiki/Simon_Coveney" title="Simon Coveney">Simon Coveney</a> as <a href="/wiki/T%C3%A1naiste" title="T\xc3\xa1naiste">T\xc3\xa1naiste</a>. It is supported by a number of independents including <a href="/wiki/Shane_Ross" title="Shane Ross">Shane Ross</a> and former Senator <a href="/wiki/Katherine_Zappone" title="Katherine Zappone">Katherine Zappone</a>. The minority government is held in place by a <a href="/wiki/Confidence_and_supply" title="Confidence and supply">confidence and supply</a> deal with Fianna F\xc3\xa1il. Opposition parties in the current <i lang="ga" title="Irish language text">D\xc3\xa1il</i> are <a href="/wiki/Fianna_F%C3%A1il" title="Fianna F\xc3\xa1il">Fianna F\xc3\xa1il</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sinn_F%C3%A9in" title="Sinn F\xc3\xa9in">Sinn F\xc3\xa9in</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(Ireland)" title="Labour Party (Ireland)">Labour Party</a>, <a href="/wiki/Solidarity%E2%80%93People_Before_Profit" title="Solidarity\xe2\x80\x93People Before Profit">Solidarity\xe2\x80\x93People Before Profit</a>,  <a href="/wiki/Social_Democrats_(Ireland)" title="Social Democrats (Ireland)">Social Democrats</a>, <a href="/wiki/Workers_and_Unemployed_Action" title="Workers and Unemployed Action">Workers and Unemployed Action</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Green_Party_(Ireland)" title="Green Party (Ireland)">Green Party</a> as well as a number of <a href="/wiki/Independent_politician" title="Independent politician">independents</a>.\n</p><p>Ireland has been a <a href="/wiki/Member_state_of_the_European_Union" title="Member state of the European Union">member state of the European Union</a> since 1973, but has chosen to remain outside the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a>. Citizens of the United Kingdom can freely enter the country without a passport due to the <a href="/wiki/Common_Travel_Area" title="Common Travel Area">Common Travel Area</a>, which is a passport-free zone comprising the islands of Ireland, Great Britain, the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man" title="Isle of Man">Isle of Man</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Channel_Islands" title="Channel Islands">Channel Islands</a>. However, some identification is required at airports and seaports.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_government">Local government</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Local_government_in_the_Republic_of_Ireland" title="Local government in the Republic of Ireland">Local government in the Republic of Ireland</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Government_buildings2_(8162790757).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Government_buildings2_%288162790757%29.jpg/220px-Government_buildings2_%288162790757%29.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Government_buildings2_%288162790757%29.jpg/330px-Government_buildings2_%288162790757%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Government_buildings2_%288162790757%29.jpg/440px-Government_buildings2_%288162790757%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3168" data-file-height="2112" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Government_buildings2_(8162790757).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Government_Buildings" title="Government Buildings">Government Buildings</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Local_Government_(Ireland)_Act_1898" title="Local Government (Ireland) Act 1898">Local Government Act 1898</a><sup id="cite_ref-LocalGovReform2014_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LocalGovReform2014-64">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> is the founding document of the present system of local government, while the <a href="/wiki/Twentieth_Amendment_of_the_Constitution_of_Ireland" title="Twentieth Amendment of the Constitution of Ireland">Twentieth Amendment to the constitution</a> of 1999 provided for its constitutional recognition. The twenty-six traditional <a href="/wiki/Counties_of_Ireland" title="Counties of Ireland">counties of Ireland</a> are not always coterminous with administrative divisions although they are generally used as a geographical frame of reference by the population of Ireland. The <a href="/wiki/Local_Government_Reform_Act_2014" title="Local Government Reform Act 2014">Local Government Reform Act 2014</a> provides for a system of <a href="/wiki/Administrative_counties_of_the_Republic_of_Ireland" class="mw-redirect" title="Administrative counties of the Republic of Ireland">thirty-one local authorities</a> - twenty-six county councils, two city and county councils and three city councils.<sup id="cite_ref-LocalGovReform2014_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LocalGovReform2014-64">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> Below this (with the exception of the Dublin Region and the three city councils) are <a href="/wiki/Municipal_district" title="Municipal district">municipal districts</a>, replacing a previous system of <a href="/wiki/Town_Councils_in_the_Republic_of_Ireland" class="mw-redirect" title="Town Councils in the Republic of Ireland">town councils</a>.\n</p>\n<center>\n<table>\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<td valign="top">\n<table style="margin:auto;" cellpadding="10">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<td><div class="floatright"><a href="/wiki/File:Ireland_Administrative_Counties.svg" class="image"><img alt="Ireland Administrative Counties.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Ireland_Administrative_Counties.svg/250px-Ireland_Administrative_Counties.svg.png" width="250" height="313" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Ireland_Administrative_Counties.svg/375px-Ireland_Administrative_Counties.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Ireland_Administrative_Counties.svg/500px-Ireland_Administrative_Counties.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="710" data-file-height="890" /></a></div>\n</td>\n<td style="font-size: 85%; font-weight:bold;">\n<ol><li><a href="/wiki/Fingal_County_Council" title="Fingal County Council">Fingal</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Dublin_City_Council" title="Dublin City Council">Dublin City</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/D%C3%BAn_Laoghaire%E2%80%93Rathdown_County_Council" title="D\xc3\xban Laoghaire\xe2\x80\x93Rathdown County Council">D\xc3\xban Laoghaire\xe2\x80\x93Rathdown</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/South_Dublin_County_Council" title="South Dublin County Council">South Dublin</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Wicklow_County_Council" title="Wicklow County Council">Wicklow</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Wexford_County_Council" title="Wexford County Council">Wexford</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Carlow_County_Council" title="Carlow County Council">Carlow</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Kildare_County_Council" title="Kildare County Council">Kildare</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Meath_County_Council" title="Meath County Council">Meath</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Louth_County_Council" title="Louth County Council">Louth</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Monaghan_County_Council" title="Monaghan County Council">Monaghan</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Cavan_County_Council" title="Cavan County Council">Cavan</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Longford_County_Council" title="Longford County Council">Longford</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Westmeath_County_Council" title="Westmeath County Council">Westmeath</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Offaly_County_Council" title="Offaly County Council">Offaly</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Laois_County_Council" title="Laois County Council">Laois</a></li></ol>\n</td>\n<td style="font-size: 85%; font-weight:bold;"><ol start="17">\n<li><a href="/wiki/Kilkenny_County_Council" title="Kilkenny County Council">Kilkenny</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Waterford_City_and_County_Council" title="Waterford City and County Council">Waterford</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Cork_City_Council" title="Cork City Council">Cork City</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Cork_County_Council" title="Cork County Council">Cork</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Kerry_County_Council" title="Kerry County Council">Kerry</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Limerick_City_and_County_Council" title="Limerick City and County Council">Limerick</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Tipperary_County_Council" title="Tipperary County Council">Tipperary</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Clare_County_Council" title="Clare County Council">Clare</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Galway_County_Council" title="Galway County Council">Galway</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Galway_City_Council" title="Galway City Council">Galway City</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Mayo_County_Council" title="Mayo County Council">Mayo</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Roscommon_County_Council" title="Roscommon County Council">Roscommon</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Sligo_County_Council" title="Sligo County Council">Sligo</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Leitrim_County_Council" title="Leitrim County Council">Leitrim</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Donegal_County_Council" title="Donegal County Council">Donegal</a></li>\n</ol>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n</center>\n<p>Local authorities are responsible for matters such as planning, local roads, sanitation, and libraries. <a href="/wiki/D%C3%A1il_constituencies" title="D\xc3\xa1il constituencies">D\xc3\xa1il constituencies</a> are required to follow county boundaries as much as possible. Counties with greater populations have multiple constituencies, some of more than one county, but generally do not cross county boundaries. The counties are grouped into eight <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_the_Republic_of_Ireland" class="mw-redirect" title="Regions of the Republic of Ireland">regions</a>, each with a Regional Authority composed of members delegated by the various county and city councils in the region. The regions do not have any direct administrative role as such, but they serve for planning, coordination and statistical purposes.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Law">Law</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Law_of_the_Republic_of_Ireland" title="Law of the Republic of Ireland">Law of the Republic of Ireland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Courts_of_the_Republic_of_Ireland" class="mw-redirect" title="Courts of the Republic of Ireland">Courts of the Republic of Ireland</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Law_enforcement_in_the_Republic_of_Ireland" title="Law enforcement in the Republic of Ireland">Law enforcement in the Republic of Ireland</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dublin_four_courts.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Dublin_four_courts.JPG/220px-Dublin_four_courts.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Dublin_four_courts.JPG/330px-Dublin_four_courts.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Dublin_four_courts.JPG/440px-Dublin_four_courts.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1632" data-file-height="1224" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dublin_four_courts.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Four_Courts" title="Four Courts">Four Courts</a>, completed in 1802, is the principal building for civil courts</div></div></div>\n<p>Ireland has a <a href="/wiki/Common_law" title="Common law">common law</a> <a href="/wiki/Legal_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Legal system">legal system</a> with a written constitution that provides for a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_democracy" class="mw-redirect" title="Parliamentary democracy">parliamentary democracy</a>.
